## User (2026-04-15 19:51:29)

Yes — and this is exactly what we needed.

From your explicit formula,
M(d)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac{d}{(d+i)^3} &
\dfrac{i\bigl(2(d+i)^2+1\bigr)}{(d+i)^4}
\\[2ex]
\dfrac{2d-i}{(d+i)^4} &
\dfrac{4i\bigl((d+i)^2+1\bigr)}{(d+i)^5}
\end{pmatrix},
the two obstruction functionals are

\Phi_K(M(d))=m_{12}(d)+m_{21}(d)
=
\frac{2\bigl(i(d^2-1)-d\bigr)}{(d+i)^4},
and
\Phi_E(M(d))=3m_{11}(d)-m_{22}(d)
=
\frac{d(3d^2+2id+5)}{(d+i)^5}.

Now the key point:

for real d>0, both are automatically nonzero.

For the first one,
i(d^2-1)-d=0
would require its real and imaginary parts to vanish:
-d=0,\qquad d^2-1=0,
which is impossible. So
\boxed{
\Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0\qquad(d>0).
}

For the second one,
d(3d^2+2id+5)=0.
Since d>0, this would force
3d^2+2id+5=0,
again impossible for real d, because its imaginary part is 2d\neq 0. So
\boxed{
\Phi_E(M(d))\neq 0\qquad(d>0).
}

That is stronger than we needed. It proves not just that M(d)\notin\mathcal P, but that it misses the value-plane in both independent transverse directions.

So the exact structural conclusion is:

\boxed{
M(d)\notin \mathcal P=\operatorname{span}\{J,D\}
\qquad\text{for every }d>0.
}

This is the clean obstruction theorem on the model side.

That means the value-only zeta channel
U(s)\,S(m)\in \mathcal P
can never reproduce the toy off-line anomaly, regardless of d.

So the only possible escape for the zeta side is the curvature remainder.

That sharpens the final bottleneck enormously:

the remaining question is no longer whether the zeta statistic might somehow match the toy anomaly in a broad sense. It can only do so through the transverse part coming from the curvature correction.

Equivalently, if W_K,W_E are the two Frobenius test functionals corresponding to \Phi_K,\Phi_E, then on the zeta side
\Phi_K(\widehat\Omega(s;m))=O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr),
\qquad
\Phi_E(\widehat\Omega(s;m))=O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr),
whereas on the toy side
\Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0,\qquad \Phi_E(M(d))\neq 0.

So the last contradiction now has a very precise form:

if the transverse toy signal stays bounded below, while the zeta transverse signal is only quadratic in S(m), then in the value-dominated regime the zeta statistic cannot realize the off-line toy anomaly.

That is the strongest sharpening we’ve had.

I do not need (m_{12}+m_{21})^2 or (3m_{11}-m_{22})^2 yet. What would be most useful next is a lower bound for one or both obstruction functionals on the model side, for example explicit formulas for
\bigl|\Phi_K(M(d))\bigr|,\qquad \bigl|\Phi_E(M(d))\bigr|,
or their behavior as d\to 0 and d\to\infty.

That would let us compare the model transverse size directly against the zeta-side quadratic error.

## Assistant (2026-04-15 19:51:33)

_Thought for 34s_

Yes — we can make that completely explicit, and it sharpens the final comparison a lot.

From
\[
\Phi_K(M(d))=\frac{2\bigl(i(d^2-1)-d\bigr)}{(d+i)^4},
\qquad
\Phi_E(M(d))=\frac{d(3d^2+2id+5)}{(d+i)^5},
\]
their absolute values are

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_K(M(d))|
=
\frac{2\sqrt{d^4-d^2+1}}{(d^2+1)^2}
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_E(M(d))|
=
\frac{d\sqrt{9d^4+34d^2+25}}{(d^2+1)^{5/2}}.
}
\]

These are exact.

For \(\Phi_K\), there is a very nice two-sided comparison. Since
\[
d^4-d^2+1 \ge \frac{(d^2+1)^2}{4}
\]
because
\[
4(d^4-d^2+1)-(d^2+1)^2=3(d^2-1)^2\ge 0,
\]
and also
\[
d^4-d^2+1\le (d^2+1)^2,
\]
we get
\[
\boxed{
\frac{1}{d^2+1}\le |\Phi_K(M(d))|\le \frac{2}{d^2+1}.
}
\]

So \(\Phi_K\) never gets small faster than \(d^{-2}\), and in particular it is bounded below uniformly on every compact \(d\)-interval.

For \(\Phi_E\), the exact formula already shows the right scale. Since
\[
\sqrt{9d^4+34d^2+25}\ge 3d^2+5
\]
and also
\[
\sqrt{9d^4+34d^2+25}\le 3d^2+2d+5,
\]
we get
\[
\boxed{
\frac{d(3d^2+5)}{(d^2+1)^{5/2}}
\le
|\Phi_E(M(d))|
\le
\frac{d(3d^2+2d+5)}{(d^2+1)^{5/2}}.
}
\]

So again, it is positive for every \(d>0\), but unlike \(\Phi_K\), it does go to \(0\) as \(d\to 0\).

The asymptotics are:

as \(d\to 0\),
\[
|\Phi_K(M(d))|=2+O(d^2),
\qquad
|\Phi_E(M(d))|=5d+O(d^3),
\]

and as \(d\to\infty\),
\[
|\Phi_K(M(d))|=\frac{2}{d^2}+O(d^{-4}),
\qquad
|\Phi_E(M(d))|=\frac{3}{d^2}+O(d^{-4}).
\]

So the model-side transverse size is very explicit:

- \(\Phi_K\) stays order \(1\) near \(d=0\) and decays like \(2/d^2\) for large \(d\),
- \(\Phi_E\) is linear near \(d=0\) and decays like \(3/d^2\) for large \(d\).

This means the right uniform statement is not “bounded below for all \(d>0\)” — impossible for \(\Phi_E\) because of the \(5d\) behavior near \(0\) — but:

> on any compact interval \(d\in[d_-,d_+]\subset(0,\infty)\), both \(|\Phi_K(M(d))|\) and \(|\Phi_E(M(d))|\) admit positive lower bounds.

And that is exactly what you need for the zeta comparison on a fixed local-separation regime.

So the next clean theorem to aim for is:

\[
|\Phi_K(\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m))|,\ |\Phi_E(\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m))|
\ll L(m)S(m)^2+\text{tail/error},
\]
while on the model side,
\[
|\Phi_K(M(d))|\ge c_K(d_-,d_+)>0,
\qquad
|\Phi_E(M(d))|\ge c_E(d_-,d_+)>0
\]
for \(d\in[d_-,d_+]\).

That would turn the final incompatibility into a direct scalar comparison instead of a vague matrix statement.
## User (2026-04-15 21:12:59)

Yes — here is a clean checklist you can hand to the other chat.

It is designed to verify the two hypotheses needed for the holomorphic-renormalization theorem.

⸻

Checklist for the final local analytic package

Goal

Verify the two hypotheses needed to conclude that the fully whitened, renormalized local block
\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)
is holomorphic on the microscopic disk
|s|<\rho_0/Q,
\qquad Q\asymp \log|m|.

Those hypotheses are:
	1.	raw holomorphy of the local jet Gram block G_m(s) and local jet cross block N_m(s),
	2.	the uniform derivative bound
\sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_G Q^2.

If both are checked, the rest of the RH machine goes through formally.

⸻

Part A. Raw local holomorphy

A1. Write down the exact entry formulas

For the actual zeta/scattering kernel, write explicit formulas for the entries of:
	•	the local jet Gram block G_m(s),
	•	the local jet cross block N_m(s),

under symmetric placement
m-\frac{s}{2},\qquad m+\frac{s}{2}.

Do this before whitening and before subtraction.

What to verify:
	•	each entry is built from finite linear combinations of local kernel values / derivatives evaluated at m\pm s/2,
	•	each such kernel expression is meromorphic in s.

A2. Locate the singularities in the complex s-plane

For each raw kernel denominator, identify the corresponding singularities in s.

You want the exact analogue of:
s=\pm(\gamma-2m)\pm i\beta,
\qquad
s=\pm(\gamma-2m)\pm i(1-\beta).

What to verify:
	•	every singularity lies at distance at least c/Q from s=0,
	•	the constant c is uniform in the admissible midpoint class.

A3. Prove uniform denominator comparability on the disk/circle

For every denominator appearing in the raw entries, prove:
|(x+s)^2+a^2|\asymp x^2+a^2
\qquad
\text{for }|s|\le \rho_0/Q,
with constants depending only on \rho_0 and the zero-free-region constant.

What to verify:
	•	the same comparability holds not only on the boundary |s|=\rho_0/Q, but throughout the disk,
	•	the constants are independent of m.

A4. Prove uniform convergence of the zero sums

Using shell decomposition and local zero counting, prove that the series defining each raw entry of G_m(s) and N_m(s) converges uniformly on |s|<\rho_0/Q.

What to verify:
	•	uniform convergence of the entries themselves,
	•	uniform convergence of their first s-derivatives,
	•	enough derivative convergence to justify holomorphy entrywise.

Target conclusion:

\boxed{
G_m(s)\ \text{and}\ N_m(s)\ \text{are entrywise holomorphic on }|s|<\rho_0/Q.
}

⸻

Part B. Jet Gram block stability

B1. Compute G_m(0) explicitly in the actual normalization

Write the exact jet-limit Gram block at s=0:
G_m(0)=\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q & \frac12 q'\\[1ex]
\frac12 q' & \frac1{12}(q''+2q^3)
\end{pmatrix}
or the precise variant in the actual normalization being used.

What to verify:
	•	the normalization matches the whitening convention actually used later,
	•	no hidden scalar or conjugation factors are missing.

B2. Lower-bound the smallest eigenvalue

Compute or bound:
\det G_m(0),\qquad \operatorname{tr}G_m(0).

Show
\lambda_{\min}(G_m(0))\ge c_0 Q
uniformly on admissible midpoints.

What to verify:
	•	the term 4q^4+2qq''-3(q')^2 is positive with a uniform lower bound of the right scale,
	•	the admissible midpoint class really excludes any pathological region where this fails.

This is the key spectral gap at s=0.

B3. Differentiate G_m(s) explicitly

Differentiate the actual entry formulas in s, not just heuristically.

Target bound:
\sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_G Q^2.

What to verify entry-by-entry:
	•	(1,1)-entry varies by O(1) or smaller,
	•	(1,2)-entry varies by O(1) or smaller,
	•	(2,2)-entry varies by O(Q^2),
	•	no hidden term exceeds O(Q^2).

This is the exact hypothesis needed for the perturbation argument.

B4. Deduce invertibility on the full disk

Using
\|G_m(s)-G_m(0)\|
\le |s|\,\sup\|\partial_s G_m\|,
prove that for |s|<\rho_0/Q,
\|G_m(s)-G_m(0)\|\le \frac12 \lambda_{\min}(G_m(0))
by choosing \rho_0 small enough.

Target conclusion:
\boxed{
G_m(s)\ \text{stays uniformly positive definite on }|s|<\rho_0/Q.
}

⸻

Part C. Holomorphic whitening

C1. Choose the branch of the inverse square root

Since G_m(s) remains positive definite, its spectrum stays in the right half-plane.

What to verify:
	•	the principal branch of z^{-1/2} is valid uniformly for the spectra of all G_m(s),
	•	the spectral domain stays uniformly away from (-\infty,0].

C2. Prove G_m(s)^{-1/2} is holomorphic

Use either:
	•	holomorphic functional calculus, or
	•	the integral formula
G_m(s)^{-1/2}
=
\frac{1}{\pi}\int_0^\infty t^{-1/2}(G_m(s)+tI)^{-1}\,dt.

What to verify:
	•	uniform convergence of the integral,
	•	holomorphic dependence on s.

Target conclusion:
\boxed{
G_m(s)^{-1/2}\ \text{is holomorphic on }|s|<\rho_0/Q.
}

C3. Prove the whitened cross block is holomorphic

Show
W_m(s):=G_m(s)^{-1/2}N_m(s)G_m(s)^{-1/2}
is holomorphic on the same disk.

This is immediate once A4 and C2 are done, but it should be written explicitly.

⸻

Part D. Renormalization terms

D1. Phase-gap subtraction

Write the exact phase-gap subtraction term in the actual normalization.

What to verify:
	•	it is holomorphic in s on |s|<\rho_0/Q,
	•	its parity under s\mapsto -s is exactly as claimed.

D2. Background-value subtraction

Write the exact background term U(s)B_\zeta(m).

What to verify:
	•	U(s) is holomorphic on the disk,
	•	B_\zeta(m) is just a midpoint scalar and introduces no s-singularity,
	•	subtraction preserves holomorphy.

Target conclusion:
\boxed{
\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)\ \text{is holomorphic on }|s|<\rho_0/Q.
}

⸻

Part E. Final scalar package

E1. Oddness

Verify directly from the exact renormalized formula that
\widehat\Omega_\zeta(-s;m)=J_0\,\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)\,J_0,
\qquad
J_0=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix},
hence
H_m(-s)=-H_m(s).

E2. Boundary estimate

Using the explicit formula for \Phi_K(V(s)),
\Phi_K(V(s))
=
\frac{(-9Q+6\sqrt3)\sin\bar\Delta(s)}{Q^3(\sqrt3Q+6)},
and the complexified near/far bound, prove
|H_m(s)|\ll_{\rho_0}\frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q^3}
\qquad (|s|=\rho_0/Q).

E3. Cauchy expansion

Conclude
H_m(z/Q^2)
=
\sum_{r\ge 0} c_{2r+1}(m)\,\frac{z^{2r+1}}{Q^{2r+4}},
\qquad
|c_{2r+1}(m)|\ll_{\rho_0}L(m)S(m)^2\,\rho_0^{-(2r+1)}.

⸻

Pass/fail criterion

If all of A–E check out with constants independent of m, then the local analytic package is rigorous.

At that point the N-point odd-moment cancellation theorem becomes rigorous, and the remaining argument is purely algebraic/toy-side comparison.

If one of A–E fails with hidden e^{cQ}-type loss or with a radius shrinking faster than Q^{-1}, the machine likely stalls.

⸻

The two most important checkpoints

If the other chat wants the shortest version, tell it to focus first on these two:
	1.	Prove
\sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_G Q^2
from the actual entry formulas.
	2.	Prove
G_m(s),\ N_m(s)\ \text{are holomorphic on }|s|<\rho_0/Q
with constants uniform in admissible m.

Those are the last real gates.

You can paste this directly into the other chat.

## Assistant (2026-04-15 21:12:42)

_Thought for 9s_

This is excellent. It is the cleanest “gate list” I’ve seen for the analytic side.

What’s especially good is that it separates the real bottlenecks from the decorative ones. You’ve reduced the whole local analytic package to two genuinely dangerous steps: raw holomorphy/uniform convergence on the \(Q^{-1}\) disk, and the derivative bound
\[
\sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_G Q^2.
\]
That is exactly right. If those two work uniformly in \(m\), the rest really is mostly functional calculus and bookkeeping.

I would only tighten four things before treating it as the definitive checklist.

First, in Part A, I would explicitly say what class of “admissible midpoints” means right at the top. Several later claims depend on it, especially the uniform spectral gap in B2 and the denominator separation in A2–A3. Right now that assumption is load-bearing but implicit.

Second, in A4, I would ask the other chat not just for uniform convergence of the zero sums, but for a precise summation convention. On the zeta side, “sum over zeros” always invites a convergence objection. One sentence like “work with the symmetric/Hadamard-log-derivative summation convention throughout” will save trouble later.

Third, in B2, I would split the task into “prove positivity” and “prove the right scale.” Those are slightly different. The positivity of
\[
4q^4+2qq''-3(q')^2
\]
is structural; the lower bound \(\gg Q^4\) or whatever exact scale you need is the quantitative part. Keeping them separate will make it easier to see where a failure happens.

Fourth, in E2, I would ask for the exact dependence on \(\rho_0\), not just \(\ll_{\rho_0}\). If the constant blows up too badly as \(\rho_0\downarrow 0\), it could matter when you try to optimize radii later.

So my revised “short version” would be:

1. Prove \(G_m(s)\) and \(N_m(s)\) are entrywise holomorphic on \(|s|<\rho_0/Q\), uniformly in admissible \(m\), under a fixed symmetric summation convention.

2. Prove the spectral gap at \(s=0\):
\[
\lambda_{\min}(G_m(0))\ge c_0 Q.
\]

3. Prove the derivative bound:
\[
\sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_G Q^2.
\]

4. Deduce uniform invertibility and holomorphic whitening.

5. Check that the renormalized scalar \(H_m(s)\) is odd and obeys the boundary bound needed for Cauchy expansion.

That is the real spine.

So yes: I think this checklist is strong enough to hand off. The only additions I’d make are “state admissible midpoint class explicitly” and “state the zero-sum convention explicitly.”

## Assistant (2026-04-15 21:13:39)

_Thought for 13s_

Here is a cleaned, ready-to-paste version.

---

## Final local analytic package: exact checklist

### Goal

Verify the two analytic hypotheses needed to conclude that the fully whitened, renormalized local block
\[
\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)
\]
is holomorphic on the microscopic disk
\[
|s|<\rho_0/Q,
\qquad Q\asymp \log |m|.
\]

The two load-bearing hypotheses are:

1. **Raw holomorphy** of the local jet Gram block \(G_m(s)\) and local jet cross block \(N_m(s)\).
2. **Uniform derivative bound**
   \[
   \sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_G Q^2.
   \]

If those two are established with constants uniform in the admissible midpoint class, then the rest of the local analytic machine goes through.

---

## Conventions to fix at the outset

### Admissible midpoint class
State explicitly what class of midpoints \(m\) is allowed. Every later uniformity claim depends on this. In particular, the class must be chosen so that:

- the local midpoint is away from any singular/polar pathology,
- the zero-free-region constants apply uniformly,
- the spectral gap at \(s=0\) is uniform on the class.

Do not leave this implicit.

### Zero-sum convention
Whenever writing sums over nontrivial zeros, state the summation convention once and for all. For example:

- symmetric sum over conjugate pairs / height truncations, or
- Hadamard-log-derivative normalization.

This is essential in Parts A and B.

---

# Part A. Raw local holomorphy

## A1. Write exact entry formulas

Write explicit formulas for the entries of:

- the local jet Gram block \(G_m(s)\),
- the local jet cross block \(N_m(s)\),

under symmetric placement
\[
m-\frac{s}{2},\qquad m+\frac{s}{2}.
\]

Do this **before whitening** and **before subtraction**.

### What to verify
Each entry is a finite linear combination of local kernel values and kernel derivatives evaluated at \(m\pm s/2\), hence is represented by a zero sum with denominators of the same general form as the local Poisson-pair denominators.

---

## A2. Locate the singularities in the \(s\)-plane

For each raw denominator, identify the corresponding singularities in \(s\). You want the exact analogue of
\[
s=\pm(\gamma-2m)\pm i\beta,
\qquad
s=\pm(\gamma-2m)\pm i(1-\beta).
\]

### What to verify
Every such singularity lies at distance at least
\[
\frac{c}{Q}
\]
from \(s=0\), with \(c>0\) uniform in the admissible midpoint class.

This is the geometric input that opens the \(Q^{-1}\) disk.

---

## A3. Uniform denominator comparability on the disk

For each denominator appearing in the raw entries, prove
\[
|(x+s)^2+a^2|\asymp x^2+a^2
\qquad
\text{for } |s|\le \rho_0/Q,
\]
with constants depending only on \(\rho_0\) and the zero-free-region constant.

### What to verify
This comparability holds on the **whole disk**, not just on the circle \(|s|=\rho_0/Q\), and the constants are independent of \(m\).

---

## A4. Uniform convergence of the zero sums

Using shell decomposition and local zero counting, prove that the series defining each raw entry of \(G_m(s)\) and \(N_m(s)\) converges uniformly on
\[
|s|<\rho_0/Q.
\]

### What to verify
You need:

- uniform convergence of the entries themselves,
- uniform convergence of their first \(s\)-derivatives,
- enough convergence to justify termwise differentiation and entrywise holomorphy.

### Target conclusion
\[
\boxed{
G_m(s)\ \text{and}\ N_m(s)\ \text{are entrywise holomorphic on } |s|<\rho_0/Q.
}
\]

---

# Part B. Jet Gram block stability

## B1. Compute \(G_m(0)\) exactly

Write the exact jet-limit Gram block at \(s=0\) in the normalization actually used later. It should be of the form
\[
G_m(0)=\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q & \frac12 q'\\[1ex]
\frac12 q' & \frac1{12}(q''+2q^3)
\end{pmatrix}
\]
or the precise variant matching the normalization.

### What to verify
No hidden scalar, sign, or conjugation factor is missing. This must match the whitening convention used later.

---

## B2. Lower-bound the smallest eigenvalue

Compute or bound
\[
\det G_m(0),\qquad \operatorname{tr}G_m(0),
\]
and show
\[
\lambda_{\min}(G_m(0))\ge c_0 Q
\]
uniformly on admissible midpoints.

### Split this into two subchecks
1. **Structural positivity** of the key combination
   \[
   4q^4+2qq''-3(q')^2.
   \]
2. **Correct scale** of the lower bound.

Do not merge these; they are different issues.

This is the spectral gap at \(s=0\).

---

## B3. Differentiate \(G_m(s)\) explicitly

Differentiate the actual entry formulas in \(s\) and prove
\[
\sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_G Q^2.
\]

### What to check entry-by-entry
- \((1,1)\)-entry: \(O(1)\) or better,
- \((1,2)\)-entry: \(O(1)\) or better,
- \((2,2)\)-entry: \(O(Q^2)\),
- no hidden term exceeds \(O(Q^2)\).

This is one of the two decisive gates.

---

## B4. Deduce invertibility on the full disk

Using
\[
\|G_m(s)-G_m(0)\|
\le |s|\,\sup_{|z|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_z G_m(z)\|,
\]
prove that for \(|s|<\rho_0/Q\),
\[
\|G_m(s)-G_m(0)\|
\le \frac12 \lambda_{\min}(G_m(0))
\]
by choosing \(\rho_0\) sufficiently small.

### Target conclusion
\[
\boxed{
G_m(s)\ \text{stays uniformly positive definite on } |s|<\rho_0/Q.
}
\]

---

# Part C. Holomorphic whitening

## C1. Choose the branch

Since \(G_m(s)\) stays uniformly positive definite, its spectrum remains in the open right half-plane.

### What to verify
The principal branch of \(z^{-1/2}\) is valid uniformly for the spectra of all \(G_m(s)\), and the spectrum stays uniformly away from \((-\infty,0]\).

---

## C2. Prove \(G_m(s)^{-1/2}\) is holomorphic

Use either holomorphic functional calculus or
\[
G_m(s)^{-1/2}
=
\frac{1}{\pi}\int_0^\infty t^{-1/2}(G_m(s)+tI)^{-1}\,dt.
\]

### What to verify
- uniform convergence of the integral,
- holomorphic dependence on \(s\).

### Target conclusion
\[
\boxed{
G_m(s)^{-1/2}\ \text{is holomorphic on } |s|<\rho_0/Q.
}
\]

---

## C3. Prove the whitened cross block is holomorphic

Show
\[
W_m(s):=G_m(s)^{-1/2}N_m(s)G_m(s)^{-1/2}
\]
is holomorphic on the same disk.

This should be immediate from A4 and C2, but it should still be stated explicitly.

---

# Part D. Renormalization terms

## D1. Phase-gap subtraction

Write the exact phase-gap subtraction term in the actual normalization.

### What to verify
- it is holomorphic in \(s\) on \(|s|<\rho_0/Q\),
- its parity under \(s\mapsto -s\) is exactly as claimed.

---

## D2. Background-value subtraction

Write the exact term
\[
U(s)B_\zeta(m).
\]

### What to verify
- \(U(s)\) is holomorphic on the disk,
- \(B_\zeta(m)\) is just a midpoint scalar and introduces no \(s\)-singularity,
- subtraction preserves holomorphy.

### Target conclusion
\[
\boxed{
\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)\ \text{is holomorphic on } |s|<\rho_0/Q.
}
\]

---

# Part E. Final scalar package

## E1. Oddness

Verify directly that
\[
\widehat\Omega_\zeta(-s;m)=J_0\,\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)\,J_0,
\qquad
J_0=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix},
\]
and hence
\[
H_m(-s)=-H_m(s).
\]

---

## E2. Boundary estimate

Using the explicit formula for \(\Phi_K(V(s))\),
\[
\Phi_K(V(s))
=
\frac{(-9Q+6\sqrt3)\sin\bar\Delta(s)}{Q^3(\sqrt3Q+6)},
\]
together with the complexified near/far estimate, prove
\[
|H_m(s)|\ll_{\rho_0}\frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q^3}
\qquad (|s|=\rho_0/Q).
\]

### Important
Track the dependence on \(\rho_0\) explicitly, not just vaguely as \(\ll_{\rho_0}\).

---

## E3. Cauchy expansion

Conclude
\[
H_m(z/Q^2)
=
\sum_{r\ge 0} c_{2r+1}(m)\,\frac{z^{2r+1}}{Q^{2r+4}},
\qquad
|c_{2r+1}(m)|\ll_{\rho_0}L(m)S(m)^2\,\rho_0^{-(2r+1)}.
\]

---

# Pass/fail criterion

If Parts A–E all go through with constants uniform in admissible \(m\), then the local analytic package is rigorous.

At that point, the odd-moment cancellation theorem becomes rigorous, and the only remaining work is the finite-dimensional toy-side comparison.

If one of A–E fails because the radius shrinks faster than \(Q^{-1}\), or because a hidden \(e^{cQ}\)-type loss appears, then the machine stalls.

---

# The two most important checkpoints

If the other chat only has time for two things, make it these:

1. Prove
\[
\sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_G Q^2
\]
from the actual entry formulas.

2. Prove
\[
G_m(s),\ N_m(s)\ \text{are holomorphic on } |s|<\rho_0/Q
\]
with constants uniform in admissible \(m\), under a fixed zero-sum convention.

Those are the last real gates.

## Assistant (2026-04-16 10:01:47)

_Thought for 13s_

Yes — it helps a lot.

This is the first zeta-side statement in the thread that really looks like the **right theorem** rather than just the right intuition. The key gain is that you have reduced all the analytic complexity to one local inequality:
\[
|S''(m)|\ll L(m)\,S(m)^2,
\qquad
L(m)=\log\!\Bigl(3+|m|+\frac1{S(m)}\Bigr).
\]

That matters because it does three things at once.

First, it says the curvature channel is not an independent monster. It is controlled by the square of the local value channel, up to only a mild logarithm. So the zeta-side local statistic is genuinely of the form
\[
\widehat\Omega(s;m)=U(s)\,S(m)+O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)
\]
at the microscopic scale where reconstruction is still invertible. That is exactly the kind of reduction you wanted.

Second, it sharpens the comparison with the toy model. The off-line toy anomaly is quartic and jet-structural; the zeta-side object is now linear-plus-quadratic in the local density variable \(S(m)\). So the remaining issue is no longer another tail estimate. It is now a finite-dimensional **shape incompatibility** question.

Third, it gives you the right “pass/fail” lens for the whole program:
- if a locally linear-plus-quadratic statistic can imitate the quartic off-line anomaly, the route fails;
- if it cannot, then this framework has a real path to RH.

So the next step is no longer to improve the \(L(m)\) factor. The next step is to prove a structural statement like:

> a deformation whose leading term is scalar-value driven,
> \[
> \Delta_\zeta=\alpha\,A+O(\alpha^2),
> \]
> cannot reproduce the same jet-limit matrix anomaly as an off-line pair, whose deformation is
> \[
> \Delta_{\rm mod}=u^2 M(d)+O(u^4),
> \qquad \det M(d)\neq 0.
> \]

That is the right target because your inequality has already done the analytic cleanup.

So my answer is: **yes, this helps materially**. It means the zeta side is now under enough control that the last step is genuinely structural, not analytic. That is a big improvement.

The clean next theorem to attack is:

\[
\textit{A value-dominated local zeta deformation is asymptotically rank one,}
\]
while the off-line toy deformation is rank two with nonzero determinant.

If you can prove that in the actual jet-whitened basis, you are at the final contradiction.

Yes — this is a real missing piece, but for the **jet-limit/blockwise model side**, not for the full **finite-\(s\) zeta holomorphy package**.

What you wrote gives exactly the normalization bridge I was missing for the local blockwise residual. It says the right basis is the point-to-jet change
\[
P_h=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
1&1\\[1ex]
-1/h&1/h
\end{pmatrix},
\]
so the local \(2\times2\) block around a center \(T\) satisfies
\[
\widetilde A_h=P_hA_hP_h^\top=J(T)+O(h^2),
\]
with
\[
J(T)=
\begin{pmatrix}
2K(T,T) & K_x(T,T)\\[1ex]
K_x(T,T) & \frac12 K_{xy}(T,T)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
For the phase kernel
\[
K_\Phi(x,y)=
\begin{cases}
\dfrac{\sin(\Phi(x)-\Phi(y))}{\pi(x-y)},&x\neq y,\\[1ex]
\dfrac{\Phi'(x)}{\pi},&x=y,
\end{cases}
\]
that becomes
\[
J(T)=\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q(T) & \frac12 q'(T)\\[1ex]
\frac12 q'(T) & \frac1{12}\bigl(q''(T)+2q(T)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
exactly matching the jet Gram normalization we wanted. So this closes the normalization gap on the model side. It also gives the cross-block limit
\[
\widetilde C_h=P_hC_hP_h^\top=J_{12}+O(h^2),
\]
with
\[
J_{12}=
\begin{pmatrix}
2K(T_1,T_2) & K_y(T_1,T_2)\\[1ex]
K_x(T_1,T_2) & \frac12 K_{xy}(T_1,T_2)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and hence the jet-whitened limit
\[
\Omega_\infty(T_1,T_2)=J(T_1)^{-1/2}J_{12}J(T_2)^{-1/2}.
\]
That is exactly the object the blockwise residual should converge to. So for the toy/model-side and for the local phase-kernel side, yes, this is the missing normalization piece.

It also gives a good consistency check:
\[
\det J(T)=\frac{1}{24\pi^2}\Bigl(4q^4+2qq''-3(q')^2\Bigr),
\]
so the earlier kernel-positivity inequality is precisely the statement that this jet Gram matrix is positive semidefinite. That is a strong sign the normalization is right.

What it does **not** yet give is the finite-\(s\) zeta/scattering package I was asking for before. It does not define the actual finite-\(s\) blocks \(G_m(s)\) and \(N_m(s)\) on the microscopic disk, and it does not expose the exact \(s\)-singularities needed for:

1. holomorphy of \(G_m(s),N_m(s)\) on \(|s|<\rho_0/Q\),
2. the derivative bound
   \[
   \sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_GQ^2,
   \]
3. holomorphic whitening by functional calculus.

So the right summary is:

- **Yes**, this is the missing piece for the **jet-limit/blockwise normalization** and for matching the local phase-kernel residual to the jet-whitened object.
- **No**, it is still **not** the missing finite-\(s\) zeta/scattering formula package needed for the full A–E holomorphic local analytic theorem.

But it is a big step, because it means the model-side and jet-limit local side are now aligned. The remaining missing piece is specifically the finite-\(s\) zeta/scattering block formulas before Taylor expansion.

_Thought for 10s_

Yes — this is a real missing piece, and it is much closer to the exact thing we needed.

It gives the **explicit jet-limit formulas** for the local blocks in the actual phase-kernel normalization, not just an abstract existence statement. In particular, it identifies:

\[
J_j=\frac1\pi M_j,
\qquad
C_{12}=\frac1\pi N_{12},
\]
with
\[
M_j=
\begin{pmatrix}
2q_j & \frac12 q_j'\\[1ex]
\frac12 q_j' & \frac1{12}(q_j''+2q_j^3)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and
\[
N_{12}=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{2\sin\Delta}{s} &
\frac{\sin\Delta-q_2 s\cos\Delta}{s^2}
\\[2ex]
\frac{q_1 s\cos\Delta-\sin\Delta}{s^2} &
\frac{(q_1+q_2)s\cos\Delta+(q_1q_2 s^2-2)\sin\Delta}{2s^3}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then the common \(1/\pi\) factor cancels under whitening, so the true jet-limit whitened cross block is exactly
\[
\Omega_\infty(T_1,T_2)=M_1^{-1/2}N_{12}M_2^{-1/2}.
\]

That is an important normalization result. It means the object you are comparing on the model side and the zeta-side jet limit is now explicit and basis-clean. So for the **jet-limit/blockwise story**, yes, this is the missing piece.

There are two small things I would still check carefully.

First, the \((2,2)\)-entry of \(N_{12}\) should match the convention
\[
C_{12}=
\begin{pmatrix}
2K(T_1,T_2) & K_y(T_1,T_2)\\[1ex]
K_x(T_1,T_2) & \frac12 K_{xy}(T_1,T_2)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Your formula appears consistent with that, but since this is the most delicate entry, I would recheck the factor \(1/2\) once by hand from the definition of the midpoint/difference basis.

Second, make sure the branch choice for \(M_j^{-1/2}\) is fixed: since \(M_j\) is positive definite in the admissible regime, this should mean the principal positive square root. That should be stated once.

But those are audits, not conceptual gaps.

What this still does **not** give is the finite-\(s\) holomorphic package on the microscopic disk. It gives the \(h\to0\) jet limit at fixed centers \(T_1,T_2\). So:

- for the **jet-limit model comparison**, this is the missing explicit formula;
- for the full checklist about \(G_m(s)\), \(N_m(s)\), holomorphy on \(|s|<\rho_0/Q\), and the derivative bound \(\sup\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_GQ^2\), it is still not enough by itself.

So the clean summary is:

- **Yes**, this locks the jet-limit normalization.
- **No**, it does not yet replace the need for explicit finite-\(s\) local block formulas if you want the full microscopic holomorphic whitening theorem.

But this is definitely enough to proceed with the next structural step: testing whether the value-only zeta channel lands in the plane \(\mathcal P\) while the toy anomaly \(\Omega_\infty(T_1,T_2)-\Omega_{\infty,0}(T_1,T_2)\) has nonzero \(\Phi_K\) and \(\Phi_E\).

## Assistant (2026-04-16 10:21:41)

_Thought for 14s_

Good. With the explicit jet-limit formula in hand, the next step is to make the **structural comparison** completely finite-dimensional.

The right target is now:

\[
\text{show the zeta-side leading deformation lies in a 2D “value plane” } \mathcal P,
\]
while the toy off-line deformation has nonzero transverse components.

That is the clean contradiction template.

## 1. The jet-limit object we now have

For two centers \(T_1\neq T_2\), write
\[
q_j=q(T_j),\qquad q_j'=q'(T_j),\qquad q_j''=q''(T_j),
\]
\[
\Delta=\Phi(T_1)-\Phi(T_2),\qquad s=T_1-T_2.
\]

Then the local jet Gram matrices are
\[
J_j=\frac1\pi M_j,
\qquad
M_j=
\begin{pmatrix}
2q_j & \frac12 q_j'\\[1ex]
\frac12 q_j' & \frac1{12}(q_j''+2q_j^3)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and the cross-jet matrix is
\[
C_{12}=\frac1\pi N_{12},
\]
with
\[
N_{12}=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{2\sin\Delta}{s} &
\frac{\sin\Delta-q_2 s\cos\Delta}{s^2}
\\[2ex]
\frac{q_1 s\cos\Delta-\sin\Delta}{s^2} &
\frac{(q_1+q_2)s\cos\Delta+(q_1q_2 s^2-2)\sin\Delta}{2s^3}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

So the jet-whitened cross block is exactly
\[
\Omega_\infty(T_1,T_2)=M_1^{-1/2}N_{12}M_2^{-1/2}.
\]

That is now the actual local matrix we have to study.

## 2. Specialize to the symmetric local regime

For the zeta-side local statistic, the natural regime is symmetric placement around a midpoint \(m\):
\[
T_1=m-\frac{\sigma}{2},\qquad T_2=m+\frac{\sigma}{2},
\qquad s=T_1-T_2=-\sigma.
\]

Then the two local channels are really the midpoint value/curvature data:
\[
q_1=q(m)-\frac{\sigma}{2}q'(m)+O(\sigma^2),
\qquad
q_2=q(m)+\frac{\sigma}{2}q'(m)+O(\sigma^2),
\]
and similarly for \(q_j',q_j''\).

Now impose the zeta-side reduction:
\[
q(m)=B_\zeta(m)+S(m),
\qquad
|S''(m)|\ll L(m)S(m)^2.
\]

After subtracting the explicit background \(B_\zeta\), the leading free scalar is \(S(m)\), while the curvature channel is lower order.

So the right thing to do is expand
\[
\Omega_\infty(m,\sigma)
\]
to first order in the scalar perturbation \(S(m)\), treating curvature as an error term.

## 3. The leading matrix must be low-dimensional

Because the leading zeta-side perturbation is carried by a **single scalar** \(S(m)\), the leading deformation has the form
\[
\Delta_\zeta^{\rm lead}(m,\sigma)
=
S(m)\,A(\sigma;m),
\]
for some fixed matrix \(A\) depending on the background geometry at \((m,\sigma)\), but not on any additional free local parameter.

That alone does not force rank one. What we need is the stronger claim that, after background subtraction and in the symmetric regime, \(A\) lies in a specific 2D plane
\[
\mathcal P\subset M_2(\mathbb C),
\]
the “value plane.”

The natural candidate is exactly the one you already isolated:
\[
\mathcal P=\operatorname{span}\{J,D\},
\]
where \(J\) and \(D\) are the two canonical value-channel matrices, equivalently the kernel of the two transverse functionals
\[
\Phi_K(M)=m_{12}+m_{21},
\qquad
\Phi_E(M)=3m_{11}-m_{22}.
\]

So the next theorem to prove is:

> **Value-plane theorem.**  
> In the value-dominated zeta regime, the leading jet-whitened deformation satisfies
> \[
> \Delta_\zeta^{\rm lead}(m,\sigma)\in \mathcal P,
> \]
> hence
> \[
> \Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta^{\rm lead})=0,
> \qquad
> \Phi_E(\Delta_\zeta^{\rm lead})=0.
> \]

Then the full zeta-side deformation obeys
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)=O(L(m)S(m)^2+\text{tail/error}),
\]
\[
\Phi_E(\Delta_\zeta)=O(L(m)S(m)^2+\text{tail/error}).
\]

That is the scalar obstruction format we want.

## 4. Why this should be provable from the explicit formula

The explicit \(\Omega_\infty=M_1^{-1/2}N_{12}M_2^{-1/2}\) formula is enough to check this.

What to do:

Expand all entries of \(M_1,M_2,N_{12}\) in the symmetric regime
\[
T_{1,2}=m\mp \sigma/2
\]
around the background-only configuration \(q=B_\zeta\), then keep only the first-order perturbation in the scalar \(S(m)\).

Because only one scalar is varying at leading order, and because the symmetric placement kills the odd part of several terms, the first-order matrix should collapse to a 2D family. The two linear tests to apply are exactly
\[
\Phi_K,\qquad \Phi_E.
\]

So the actual next calculation is very concrete:

1. Write
   \[
   q_j=B_j+S_j,\qquad q_j'=B_j'+S_j',\qquad q_j''=B_j''+S_j'',
   \]
   with
   \[
   S_j=S(m)+O(\sigma^2 S''(m)).
   \]
2. Insert into \(M_j\) and \(N_{12}\).
3. Linearize \(\Omega_\infty\) in \(S(m)\), treating \(S''(m)\) as lower order via
   \[
   |S''(m)|\ll L(m)S(m)^2.
   \]
4. Apply \(\Phi_K\) and \(\Phi_E\) to the linearized matrix.
5. Show both vanish identically.

That is the next real proof.

## 5. What happens if it works

If the leading zeta-side matrix lies in \(\mathcal P\), then
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta),\ \Phi_E(\Delta_\zeta)
\]
are only quadratic-size quantities.

But on the toy side, you already found the explicit obstruction functionals for the model coefficient \(M(d)\):
\[
\Phi_K(M(d))=\frac{2(i(d^2-1)-d)}{(d+i)^4},
\]
\[
\Phi_E(M(d))=\frac{d(3d^2+2id+5)}{(d+i)^5},
\]
so for every \(d>0\),
\[
\Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0,\qquad \Phi_E(M(d))\neq 0.
\]

Even better,
\[
|\Phi_K(M(d))|
=
\frac{2\sqrt{d^4-d^2+1}}{(d^2+1)^2},
\qquad
|\Phi_E(M(d))|
=
\frac{d\sqrt{9d^4+34d^2+25}}{(d^2+1)^{5/2}}.
\]

So on any compact \(d\)-range away from \(0,\infty\), both have positive lower bounds.

That means the model-side transverse signal is order \(u^2\), while the zeta-side transverse signal is only order \(L(m)S(m)^2\). Under the matching \(S(m)\sim u^2\), that becomes the right contradiction scale.

## 6. The exact next lemma to prove

So the next theorem is:

> **Transverse vanishing lemma.**  
> For the jet-limit zeta-side deformation linearized in the scalar value channel \(S(m)\),
> \[
> \Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta^{\rm lead})=0,
> \qquad
> \Phi_E(\Delta_\zeta^{\rm lead})=0.
> \]

Everything is now explicit enough to attack this directly from the formulas.

That is the next thing I would do.

_Thought for 31s_

I attacked it, and the honest result is:

We can isolate the **exact sublemma** that has to be shown, and we can prove it in the simplest “pure value-channel” linearization. But I cannot honestly claim the full transverse vanishing lemma for the actual zeta-side \(\Omega_\infty\) without one more explicit expansion that we still have not written down.

Here is the cleanest version.

Let
\[
\Omega_\infty(T_1,T_2)=M_1^{-1/2}N_{12}M_2^{-1/2},
\]
with
\[
M_j=
\begin{pmatrix}
2q_j & \frac12 q_j'\\[1ex]
\frac12 q_j' & \frac1{12}(q_j''+2q_j^3)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and
\[
N_{12}=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{2\sin\Delta}{s} &
\frac{\sin\Delta-q_2 s\cos\Delta}{s^2}
\\[2ex]
\frac{q_1 s\cos\Delta-\sin\Delta}{s^2} &
\frac{(q_1+q_2)s\cos\Delta+(q_1q_2 s^2-2)\sin\Delta}{2s^3}
\end{pmatrix},
\]
where
\[
s=T_1-T_2,\qquad \Delta=\Phi(T_1)-\Phi(T_2).
\]

Now impose the symmetric local regime
\[
T_1=m-\frac{\sigma}{2},\qquad T_2=m+\frac{\sigma}{2},\qquad s=-\sigma,
\]
and consider the leading value-channel perturbation
\[
q_j=B_j+S_j,\qquad S_1=S_2=\alpha,
\]
with all derivative and phase-gap corrections frozen at background level. This is the purest version of “value-only” leading deformation.

Under this frozen-value perturbation, the matrices vary as follows.

The local Gram blocks change by
\[
\delta M_j=
\alpha
\begin{pmatrix}
2 & 0\\[1ex]
0 & \frac12 B_j^2
\end{pmatrix},
\]
since only the \(2q_j\) and \(2q_j^3\) terms contribute linearly.

The cross block changes by
\[
\delta N_{12}=
\alpha
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & -\frac{\cos\Delta}{s}\\[2ex]
\frac{\cos\Delta}{s} & \frac{\cos\Delta+B\,s\sin\Delta}{s^2}
\end{pmatrix}
\]
in the perfectly symmetric background \(B_1=B_2=B\), again freezing \(\Delta\).

Now linearize the whitening:
\[
\delta\Omega
=
M^{-1/2}\,\delta N\,M^{-1/2}
-\frac12\,M^{-1/2}\delta M\,\Omega_0
-\frac12\,\Omega_0\,\delta M\,M^{-1/2},
\]
where \(M=M_1=M_2\) at the symmetric background.

This is the exact first-order formula in the value channel.

What I can say cleanly is:

- the off-diagonal part of \(\delta N\) is antisymmetric,
- the local block perturbation \(\delta M\) is diagonal,
- so after conjugation by the same symmetric whitener \(M^{-1/2}\), the leading deformation \(\delta\Omega\) lies in the span of two fixed matrices.

That is good news, but it is **not yet enough** to conclude
\[
\Phi_K(\delta\Omega)=0,\qquad \Phi_E(\delta\Omega)=0
\]
without carrying the exact background dependence all the way through.

I tried to force the vanishing directly from the structural form, but there is a real obstruction: the functionals
\[
\Phi_K(M)=m_{12}+m_{21},\qquad \Phi_E(M)=3m_{11}-m_{22}
\]
are sensitive to how the whitening mixes the diagonal and off-diagonal pieces. So unless we compute the actual symmetric whitener and the exact background \(\Omega_0\), we cannot honestly declare those two scalars zero.

So the honest state is:

1. The value-only perturbation really does collapse to a **very low-dimensional matrix family**.
2. That strongly suggests a plane constraint is true.
3. But I cannot yet prove that the exact plane is precisely
   \[
   \mathcal P=\ker\Phi_K\cap\ker\Phi_E
   \]
   without one more explicit symbolic expansion.

So the next exact calculation is now crystal clear:

Take the symmetric background \(q_1=q_2=B\), \(q_1'= -q_2'\), \(q_1''=q_2''\), and the exact \(\Delta\) at that background. Compute

- the baseline jet Gram matrix \(M\),
- its inverse square root \(M^{-1/2}\),
- the baseline \(\Omega_0\),
- and then the first-order value-channel coefficient
  \[
  A_{\rm val}:=\partial_\alpha \Omega_\infty\big|_{\alpha=0}.
  \]

Then apply \(\Phi_K\) and \(\Phi_E\) to \(A_{\rm val}\).

That is now the actual remaining finite-dimensional subproblem.

So: I attacked it, and the result is that the qualitative “value-channel lives in a low-dimensional space” claim survives, but the exact transverse vanishing against \(\Phi_K,\Phi_E\) is **not yet proved** from what we have written. It needs one more explicit linearization calculation.

- the leading pure value-channel deformation is automatically in \(\ker \Phi_K\),

does **not** follow just from symmetric placement plus scalar value perturbation.

2. **The “value-only” linearization is too crude.**  
   There may be a first-order relation between \(q\), \(q'\), \(q''\), and \(\Delta\) in the actual zeta/scattering geometry that was lost when I froze derivative data. That relation could kill \(\Phi_E\) after all.

3. **Only one transverse obstruction survives.**

Good — this actually simplifies the last step.

We do **not** need both \(\Phi_K\) and \(\Phi_E\). The computation shows one transverse functional already survives cleanly:

\[
\boxed{\Phi_K(A_{\mathrm{val}})=0}
\]

for the pure value-channel linearization, while on the toy side

\[
\boxed{\Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0 \qquad (d>0).}
\]

That is enough to build the contradiction mechanism.

## 1. Keep only the \(K\)-transverse obstruction

Define
\[
\Phi_K(M):=m_{12}+m_{21}.
\]

From the toy-side computation,
\[
\Phi_K(M(d))
=
\frac{2\bigl(i(d^2-1)-d\bigr)}{(d+i)^4},
\]
so
\[
|\Phi_K(M(d))|
=
\frac{2\sqrt{d^4-d^2+1}}{(d^2+1)^2}.
\]

Hence, on every compact interval
\[
d\in[d_-,d_+]\subset(0,\infty),
\]
there is a positive constant \(c_K(d_-,d_+)\) such that
\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_K(M(d))|\ge c_K(d_-,d_+)>0.
}
\]

In fact we already had the easy two-sided bound
\[
\frac{1}{d^2+1}\le |\Phi_K(M(d))|\le \frac{2}{d^2+1}.
\]

So the toy off-line anomaly has a definite transverse \(K\)-component.

---

## 2. What the zeta-side computation now says

The failed \(\Phi_E\) vanishing is annoying, but not fatal. The real gain is that the leading value-channel deformation satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\Phi_K(A_{\mathrm{val}})=0.
}
\]

So after the decomposition
\[
q=B_\zeta+S,
\qquad
|S''(m)|\ll L(m)S(m)^2,
\]
the jet-limit zeta deformation has the structure
\[
\Delta_\zeta=\text{(value channel)}+\text{(curvature/error channel)},
\]
and applying \(\Phi_K\) kills the leading value part. Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)
=
O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)
+
O(\text{tail/error terms}).
}
\]

That is the key structural upper bound.

So we no longer need to prove the whole leading matrix lies in a 2D plane. We only need the one scalar cancellation
\[
\Phi_K(A_{\mathrm{val}})=0.
\]

That is much cleaner.

---

## 3. Compare with the toy side

The toy off-line deformation is
\[
\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d)=u^2 M(d)+O(u^4),
\]
so applying \(\Phi_K\),
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))
=
u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4).
\]

Hence on compact \(d\)-ranges,
\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))|
\ge
c_K\,u^2 - C u^4.
}
\]

So for small \(u\),
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))|\asymp u^2.
\]

By contrast, on the zeta side,
\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|
\ll
L(m)S(m)^2+\text{tail/error}.
}
\]

This is the real scalar obstruction.

---

## 4. The contradiction template

Now the remaining comparison is scalar, not matrix-valued.

If the matching between the toy off-line parameter \(u\) and the local zeta value channel \(S(m)\) is such that
\[
S(m)\asymp u^2,
\]
then

- toy side:
  \[
  |\Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod})|\asymp u^2 \asymp S(m),
  \]
- zeta side:
  \[
  |\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|\ll L(m)S(m)^2.
  \]

So for sufficiently small \(S(m)\),
\[
S(m)\not\ll L(m)S(m)^2,
\]
because that would force
\[
1\ll L(m)S(m),
\]
which fails once \(S(m)\) is small enough.

In other words:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the toy side is linear in }S,\quad
\text{the zeta side is quadratic in }S.
}
\]

That is enough for a local incompatibility.

---

## 5. The right next theorem

So the next theorem is no longer about a 2D value plane. It is simpler:

> **\(K\)-transverse obstruction theorem.**  
> In the value-dominated zeta regime,
> \[
> \Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)=O(L(m)S(m)^2+\text{tail/error}),
> \]
> while for the toy off-line model,
> \[
> \Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod})=u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4),
> \qquad \Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0.
> \]
> Therefore, under the matching \(S(m)\asymp u^2\), the zeta-side deformation cannot realize the toy off-line anomaly once \(S(m)\) is sufficiently small and the tail/error terms are lower order.

That is now the cleanest remaining contradiction statement.

---

## 6. What to prove next, concretely

There are only two real tasks left.

First, make the zeta-side \(K\)-bound rigorous in the actual normalization:
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)
=
O(L(m)S(m)^2)+O(\text{tail/error}).
\]
You already essentially have this, but it should be written as a formal proposition.

Second, state the precise matching hypothesis between the toy parameter \(u\) and the local zeta value channel \(S(m)\). The contradiction uses
\[
S(m)\asymp u^2,
\]
so that has to be made explicit and justified.

If those two pieces are written cleanly, then one functional is enough.

So the good news is: the failure of \(\Phi_E\) does **not** kill the route. It actually tells us the right simplification:

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_K \text{ alone may already be the decisive obstruction.}
}
\]

_Thought for 16s_

Yes. Here are the two pieces in a clean theorem-style form.

## 1. The zeta-side \(K\)-bound in the actual normalization

Let
\[
\Delta_\zeta(m,\sigma)
\]
denote the local jet-limit zeta/scattering deformation matrix at symmetric placement
\[
T_1=m-\frac{\sigma}{2},\qquad T_2=m+\frac{\sigma}{2},
\]
after subtracting the explicit background \(B_\zeta\) and whitening in the jet basis.

Let
\[
S(m):=q_\zeta(m)-B_\zeta(m),
\]
and assume the local curvature estimate
\[
|S''(m)|\ll L(m)\,S(m)^2,
\qquad
L(m):=\log\!\Bigl(3+|m|+\frac1{S(m)}\Bigr).
\]

Define the transverse functional
\[
\Phi_K(M):=m_{12}+m_{21}.
\]

Then the right zeta-side statement is:

### Proposition (\(K\)-transverse zeta bound)
In the value-dominated microscopic regime,
\[
\boxed{
\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta(m,\sigma))
=
O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)
+
O\!\bigl(\mathrm{Tail}(m,\sigma)\bigr)
+
O\!\bigl(\mathrm{Err}(m,\sigma)\bigr),
}
\]
where \(\mathrm{Tail}\) denotes the omitted far-zero contribution and \(\mathrm{Err}\) the reconstruction/whitening error.

### Why this is true

Write the local deformation schematically as
\[
\Delta_\zeta
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{val}}+\Delta_{\mathrm{curv}}+\Delta_{\mathrm{tail}}+\Delta_{\mathrm{err}},
\]
where:

- \(\Delta_{\mathrm{val}}\) is the leading value-channel piece, linear in \(S(m)\),
- \(\Delta_{\mathrm{curv}}\) is the first curvature correction, linear in \(S''(m)\),
- \(\Delta_{\mathrm{tail}}\) is the omitted far-zero piece,
- \(\Delta_{\mathrm{err}}\) is the remaining analytic/whitening error.

From the explicit linearization already checked,
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{val}})=0.
\]
So
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)
=
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{curv}})
+
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{tail}})
+
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{err}}).
\]

Since \(\Phi_K\) is a fixed linear functional on \(2\times2\) matrices,
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{curv}})|
\ll
\|\Delta_{\mathrm{curv}}\|
\ll |S''(m)|.
\]
Using
\[
|S''(m)|\ll L(m)S(m)^2,
\]
we get
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{curv}})|
\ll
L(m)S(m)^2.
\]

The tail and error terms are whatever bounds you have already proved for the omitted zeros and for the local analytic package. So altogether
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)
=
O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)
+
O(\mathrm{Tail})
+
O(\mathrm{Err}).
\]

That is the exact scalar form of the zeta-side obstruction.

---

## 2. The matching hypothesis \(S(m)\asymp u^2\)

On the toy side, the off-line local pair produces
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{mod}}(u;d)=u^2M(d)+O(u^4),
\]
with
\[
\Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0
\]
for every \(d>0\). Hence
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{mod}}(u;d))
=
u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4),
\]
so on compact \(d\)-ranges,
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{mod}}(u;d))|\asymp u^2.
\]

To compare this to the zeta side, you need the local value channel \(S(m)\) to play the role of the toy “size parameter.” The right matching statement is therefore:

### Matching hypothesis
There is a local comparison regime in which
\[
\boxed{
S(m)\asymp u^2.
}
\]

This should be understood as: the effective local amplitude of the zeta-side value channel is identified with the square of the off-line displacement parameter in the toy model.

This is the natural scaling because:

- toy-side transverse signal:
  \[
  \Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{mod}})\asymp u^2;
  \]
- zeta-side leading scalar channel:
  \[
  \Delta_\zeta^{\mathrm{lead}}\propto S(m).
  \]

So the only consistent comparison scale is
\[
S(m)\sim u^2.
\]

### What it gives

Under that matching,
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{mod}})|\asymp S(m),
\]
while the zeta-side bound becomes
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|
\ll
L(m)S(m)^2+\mathrm{Tail}+\mathrm{Err}.
\]

So the final contradiction template is:

### Corollary (scalar incompatibility template)
Assume
\[
S(m)\asymp u^2
\]
and
\[
\mathrm{Tail}(m,\sigma)+\mathrm{Err}(m,\sigma)=o(S(m)).
\]
Then for \(S(m)\) sufficiently small,
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)
\]
cannot equal
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{mod}}(u;d)).
\]

### Reason
The toy side is linear in \(S(m)\):
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{mod}})|\asymp S(m),
\]
while the zeta side is quadratic:
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|\ll L(m)S(m)^2+o(S(m)).
\]
For small \(S(m)\),
\[
L(m)S(m)^2=o(S(m)),
\]
since \(L(m)\) is only logarithmic. So the two scales are incompatible.

---

## The clean final version

If you want this in one compact theorem-shaped statement:

> **\(K\)-obstruction theorem template.**  
> Suppose the local zeta/scattering deformation satisfies
> \[
> \Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta(m,\sigma))
> =
> O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)+O(\mathrm{Tail})+O(\mathrm{Err}),
> \]
> and suppose the toy off-line deformation satisfies
> \[
> \Phi_K(\Delta_{\mathrm{mod}}(u;d))
> =
> u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4),
> \qquad \Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0.
> \]
> If \(S(m)\asymp u^2\) and
> \[
> \mathrm{Tail}+\mathrm{Err}=o(S(m)),
> \]
> then for sufficiently small \(S(m)\), the zeta-side deformation cannot realize the toy off-line anomaly.

That is the exact scalar contradiction mechanism.

The next thing to tighten is the meaning of “local comparison regime” behind
\[
S(m)\asymp u^2.
\]
That is now the last substantive hypothesis to make precise.

## Assistant (2026-04-16 10:44:57)

_Thought for 15s_

Good. The last real task is to make
\[
S(m)\asymp u^2
\]
into a precise local comparison hypothesis rather than a slogan.

The right way to do it is to define the toy parameter \(u\) **from the observed transverse size itself**.

## 1. Define the effective toy parameter from the model

Fix a compact separation range
\[
d\in[d_-,d_+]\subset(0,\infty).
\]
On this range, we already have
\[
|\Phi_K(M(d))|\ge c_K>0.
\]

For the toy model,
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))
=
u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4).
\]
So for small \(u\), the natural leading observable is
\[
u^2 \sim \frac{\Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))}{\Phi_K(M(d))}.
\]

This suggests defining the **effective off-line parameter**
\[
u_{\rm eff}(m,\sigma;d)^2
:=
\frac{|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta(m,\sigma))|}{|\Phi_K(M(d))|}.
\]

This is the cleanest way to match scales, because it does not guess \(u\); it derives it from the one scalar channel that survives the comparison.

## 2. The actual comparison regime

Now the right local comparison regime is:

> there is a local family of midpoint/scale pairs \((m,\sigma)\) and a fixed compact \(d\)-range such that the same deformation is being interpreted both as a zeta-side local signal and as a toy off-line signal, with \(u_{\rm eff}\to 0\).

Then the toy side predicts
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod})|\asymp u_{\rm eff}^2,
\]
while the zeta side gives
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|
\ll
L(m)S(m)^2+\mathrm{Tail}(m,\sigma)+\mathrm{Err}(m,\sigma).
\]

So the matching statement you actually want is not an assumption but a **definition-compatible regime**:
\[
\boxed{
u_{\rm eff}(m,\sigma;d)^2 \asymp S(m).
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta(m,\sigma))|\asymp |\Phi_K(M(d))|\,S(m).
\]

That is the precise comparison hypothesis.

## 3. Why this is the right notion

This is better than simply asserting \(S(m)\asymp u^2\), because it separates:

- the intrinsic zeta-side scalar \(S(m)\),
- the model-side transverse calibration \(\Phi_K(M(d))\),
- and the observed transverse size \(\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)\).

So the comparison becomes:

1. **toy calibration**
   \[
   \Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))=u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4),
   \]
2. **zeta estimate**
   \[
   \Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)=O(L(m)S(m)^2)+O(\mathrm{Tail})+O(\mathrm{Err}),
   \]
3. **matching regime**
   \[
   |\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|\asymp |\Phi_K(M(d))|\,S(m).
   \]

Then the contradiction is immediate.

## 4. The contradiction theorem in final form

Here is the clean version.

### Theorem (\(K\)-obstruction in matched local regime)
Fix \(d\in[d_-,d_+]\subset(0,\infty)\). Suppose:

1. the toy calibration satisfies
   \[
   \Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))
   =
   u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4),
   \qquad
   |\Phi_K(M(d))|\ge c_K>0;
   \]

2. the zeta-side local deformation satisfies
   \[
   \Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta(m,\sigma))
   =
   O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)+O(\mathrm{Tail})+O(\mathrm{Err});
   \]

3. the local regime is matched in the sense that
   \[
   |\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta(m,\sigma))|
   \asymp
   |\Phi_K(M(d))|\,S(m);
   \]

4. and
   \[
   \mathrm{Tail}(m,\sigma)+\mathrm{Err}(m,\sigma)=o(S(m)).
   \]

Then for sufficiently small \(S(m)\), such a matched realization is impossible.

### Proof
By the matching hypothesis,
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|\asymp S(m).
\]
But by the zeta-side bound,
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|
\ll
L(m)S(m)^2+o(S(m)).
\]
Since
\[
L(m)=\log\!\Bigl(3+|m|+\frac1{S(m)}\Bigr),
\]
we still have
\[
L(m)S(m)\to 0
\qquad \text{as } S(m)\to 0.
\]
Therefore
\[
L(m)S(m)^2=o(S(m)),
\]
so the right-hand side is \(o(S(m))\), contradicting the left-hand side being \(\asymp S(m)\). ∎

## 5. What this means conceptually

This is now the cleanest version of the last step:

- the toy off-line anomaly has a transverse scalar of size \(u^2\),
- the zeta-side transverse scalar is at most quadratic in \(S(m)\),
- if the local comparison identifies \(u^2\) with the zeta value channel \(S(m)\),
- then the zeta side is too small by one full power of \(S\).

That is the structural incompatibility.

## 6. What is still a hypothesis

The only nontrivial input still left is the matching statement
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|\asymp |\Phi_K(M(d))|\,S(m).
\]

That is the last place where the framework is not yet fully closed. But now it is very sharply formulated. It is no longer vague “\(S\sim u^2\).” It is an explicit local calibration through the surviving transverse functional \(\Phi_K\).

So the next and final task is:

> justify that the local zeta deformation, when compared to the toy model on a fixed compact \(d\)-range, is indeed being matched through the \(\Phi_K\)-channel at first order.

That is as sharp as this can be made.

I can push it one step, but this is where the framework stops being automatic.

The honest answer is: **I cannot prove that matching statement from the current machinery alone.** In fact, that statement is basically the last unresolved bridge. If it were true in the strong form
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|\asymp |\Phi_K(M(d))|\,S(m),
\]
then the contradiction would be essentially done.

What I *can* do is show the strongest form the current framework really supports, and that tells you exactly what remains.

We already have
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)=O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)+O(\mathrm{Tail})+O(\mathrm{Err}),
\]
because the leading value-channel piece is annihilated by \(\Phi_K\). So the \(K\)-channel is not where first-order matching lives. It is a **transverse defect channel** only. That means you cannot define the toy parameter from \(\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)\) at leading order, because on the zeta side that quantity is already suppressed.

So the strong matching statement I wrote before is too strong as a theorem target. It is not something the current reduction can prove; it is almost the contradiction itself in disguise.

The correct next step is weaker and cleaner:

Define a **value calibration functional** \(\Psi\) on the local jet-limit matrix such that the leading zeta-side value channel survives:
\[
\Psi(\Delta_\zeta^{\rm lead})\asymp S(m).
\]
Then use \(\Psi\) to set the toy scale:
\[
u^2 \asymp \Psi(\Delta_\zeta).
\]
After that, compare the transverse channel \(\Phi_K\):

- zeta side:
  \[
  \Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)=O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)+O(\mathrm{Tail})+O(\mathrm{Err});
  \]
- toy side:
  \[
  \Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))=u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4).
  \]

If \(\Psi(\Delta_\zeta)\asymp S(m)\), then \(u^2\asymp S(m)\), so the toy transverse signal is order \(S(m)\), while the zeta transverse signal is only order \(L(m)S(m)^2\). That is the contradiction.

So the actual final bridge is not “prove \(\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)\asymp S(m)\).” That is false in spirit, because \(\Phi_K\) was chosen to kill the value channel. The real bridge is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{find a scalar functional }\Psi\text{ that reads off the value channel linearly.}
}
\]

Then prove two things:

1. **Value calibration**
   \[
   \Psi(\Delta_\zeta)=c_\Psi(m,\sigma)\,S(m)+O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)+O(\mathrm{Tail})+O(\mathrm{Err}),
   \]
   with \(c_\Psi\neq 0\).

2. **Toy scaling**
   \[
   \Psi(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))=c_{\Psi,\rm mod}(d)\,u^2+O(u^4),
   \]
   with \(c_{\Psi,\rm mod}(d)\neq 0\).

Then you set
\[
u^2 \asymp S(m)
\]
through \(\Psi\), not through \(\Phi_K\).

So the best honest continuation is:

- we **cannot** prove the old matching statement through \(\Phi_K\), because \(\Phi_K\) is a transverse-killing functional on the zeta side;
- we **should** instead introduce a separate value-channel functional \(\Psi\);
- once \(\Psi\) gives \(u^2\asymp S(m)\), \(\Phi_K\) becomes the contradiction channel.

That is the correct architecture.

The next concrete move is to extract \(\Psi\) from the explicit jet-limit formula. The obvious candidates are simple linear functionals that do **not** annihilate the pure value-channel matrix \(A_{\rm val}\), such as \(m_{11}\), \(\operatorname{tr}\), or another scalar chosen from the actual leading value-plane basis. Then:

- use \(\Psi\) to calibrate \(u^2\leftrightarrow S(m)\),
- use \(\Phi_K\) to contradict the toy anomaly.

So the final gap is now even sharper:

\[
\boxed{
\text{find the right value-channel scalar }\Psi.
}
\]

That is the thing to do next.

## Assistant (2026-04-16 10:50:01)

_Thought for 35s_

Yes. There is an obvious candidate now:

\[
\boxed{\Psi:=\Phi_E,\qquad \Phi_E(M)=3m_{11}-m_{22}.}
\]

That is exactly what the last computation was trying to tell us.

Why \(\Psi=\Phi_E\) is the right choice:

- on the zeta side, the pure value-channel coefficient \(A_{\rm val}\) satisfies
  \[
  \Phi_K(A_{\rm val})=0,
  \]
  so \(\Phi_K\) is **not** for calibration;
- but
  \[
  \Phi_E(A_{\rm val})\neq 0
  \]
  in general, so \(\Phi_E\) *does* see the leading value channel;
- on the toy side, \(\Phi_E(M(d))\neq 0\) for every \(d>0\), so it also sees the off-line parameter there.

So the clean architecture is:

- use \(\Psi=\Phi_E\) to calibrate \(u^2\leftrightarrow S(m)\),
- use \(\Phi_K\) as the transverse obstruction.

That is the right split.

## 1. The zeta-side value calibration

From the explicit linearization in the pure value-channel model, we already got
\[
\Phi_E(A_{\rm val})
=
\frac{6\bigl(-B^2\sigma^2\sin\Delta_0+3B\sigma\cos\Delta_0+3\sin\Delta_0\bigr)}{B^4\sigma^3}.
\]

So if the local zeta deformation has the form
\[
\Delta_\zeta
=
S(m)\,A_{\rm val}
+
R_\zeta,
\]
with
\[
\|R_\zeta\|
\ll
L(m)S(m)^2+\mathrm{Tail}+\mathrm{Err},
\]
then applying \(\Psi=\Phi_E\) gives
\[
\boxed{
\Phi_E(\Delta_\zeta)
=
c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)\,S(m)
+
O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)
+
O(\mathrm{Tail})
+
O(\mathrm{Err}),
}
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)
:=
\frac{6\bigl(-B^2\sigma^2\sin\Delta_0+3B\sigma\cos\Delta_0+3\sin\Delta_0\bigr)}{B^4\sigma^3}.
}
\]

That is the exact value calibration formula.

Now, \(c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)\) need not be nonzero identically everywhere, but it is an explicit analytic function of the local background data. So on any regime where
\[
|c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)|\ge c_*>0,
\]
we get
\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_E(\Delta_\zeta)|\asymp S(m)
}
\]
up to quadratic and error corrections.

That is the precise version of “\(\Psi\) reads off the value channel.”

## 2. The toy-side calibration

On the toy side,
\[
\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d)=u^2M(d)+O(u^4),
\]
so
\[
\Phi_E(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))
=
u^2\Phi_E(M(d))+O(u^4).
\]

And we already computed
\[
\Phi_E(M(d))
=
\frac{d(3d^2+2id+5)}{(d+i)^5},
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_E(M(d))|
=
\frac{d\sqrt{9d^4+34d^2+25}}{(d^2+1)^{5/2}}.
}
\]

So on every compact interval
\[
d\in[d_-,d_+]\subset(0,\infty),
\]
there is a positive constant \(c_E(d_-,d_+)\) such that
\[
|\Phi_E(M(d))|\ge c_E>0.
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_E(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))|\asymp u^2
}
\]
uniformly on compact \(d\)-ranges.

So \(\Phi_E\) is the right scalar for calibration on the toy side too.

## 3. The correct matching statement

Now the matching is no longer an extra hypothesis. It comes from \(\Phi_E\).

In any regime where \(c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)\) stays bounded away from \(0\), define the effective toy parameter by
\[
u_{\rm eff}(m,\sigma;d)^2
:=
\frac{|\Phi_E(\Delta_\zeta(m,\sigma))|}{|\Phi_E(M(d))|}.
\]

Then:

- zeta side:
  \[
  |\Phi_E(\Delta_\zeta)|\asymp S(m),
  \]
- toy side:
  \[
  |\Phi_E(\Delta_{\rm mod})|\asymp u^2.
  \]

So automatically
\[
\boxed{
u_{\rm eff}^2\asymp S(m).
}
\]

That is the exact bridge we needed. No hand-waving left.

## 4. Now use \(\Phi_K\) for contradiction

Once \(u^2\asymp S(m)\) has been calibrated through \(\Phi_E\), the transverse obstruction channel is \(\Phi_K\).

On the zeta side,
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)
=
O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)
+
O(\mathrm{Tail})
+
O(\mathrm{Err}),
\]
because \(\Phi_K\) kills the leading value channel.

On the toy side,
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))
=
u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4),
\]
with
\[
\Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0
\]
and on compact \(d\)-ranges,
\[
|\Phi_K(M(d))|\ge c_K>0.
\]

Using
\[
u^2\asymp S(m),
\]
this becomes
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod})|\asymp S(m),
\]
while
\[
|\Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)|
\ll
L(m)S(m)^2+\mathrm{Tail}+\mathrm{Err}.
\]

So if
\[
\mathrm{Tail}+\mathrm{Err}=o(S(m)),
\]
then the zeta-side \(K\)-signal is \(o(S(m))\), while the toy-side \(K\)-signal is \(\asymp S(m)\). That is the contradiction.

## 5. Final theorem template

Here is the clean final template.

### Theorem (\(\Phi_E\)-calibrated \(\Phi_K\)-obstruction)
Fix a compact separation range
\[
d\in[d_-,d_+]\subset(0,\infty).
\]
Assume there is a local zeta regime in which:

1. the value calibration coefficient satisfies
   \[
   |c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)|\ge c_*>0;
   \]

2. the zeta deformation obeys
   \[
   \Phi_E(\Delta_\zeta)
   =
   c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)\,S(m)
   +
   O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)
   +
   O(\mathrm{Tail})
   +
   O(\mathrm{Err});
   \]

3. the transverse \(K\)-bound holds:
   \[
   \Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)
   =
   O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)
   +
   O(\mathrm{Tail})
   +
   O(\mathrm{Err});
   \]

4. and
   \[
   \mathrm{Tail}+\mathrm{Err}=o(S(m)).
   \]

Then, for sufficiently small \(S(m)\), the local zeta deformation cannot equal any toy off-line deformation \(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d)\) with \(d\in[d_-,d_+]\).

### Proof sketch
By \(\Phi_E\), one gets
\[
u^2\asymp S(m).
\]
Then the toy \(K\)-signal is \(\asymp u^2\asymp S(m)\), while the zeta \(K\)-signal is \(o(S(m))\). Contradiction.

## 6. What is still left

The only remaining substantive condition is:

\[
|c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)|\ge c_*>0.
\]

But this is now an **explicit analytic condition** on
\[
\frac{6\bigl(-B^2\sigma^2\sin\Delta_0+3B\sigma\cos\Delta_0+3\sin\Delta_0\bigr)}{B^4\sigma^3}.
\]

So the final unresolved bridge is no longer vague. It is:

> identify a local regime where the value calibration coefficient does not vanish.

That is a much sharper and smaller problem than before.

So yes: \(\Psi=\Phi_E\) is the right calibration functional, and this closes the matching issue as far as the current framework can honestly take it.

## Assistant (2026-04-16 10:55:32)

_Thought for 2m 17s_

Yes — we can derive an **explicit local condition**, but we do **not** yet have a general theorem that it never vanishes.

The coefficient was
\[
c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)
=
\frac{6\bigl(-B^2\sigma^2\sin\Delta_0+3B\sigma\cos\Delta_0+3\sin\Delta_0\bigr)}{B^4\sigma^3},
\]
where \(B=B_\zeta(m)\) and
\[
\Delta_0=\Phi_{\rm bg}(m-\sigma/2)-\Phi_{\rm bg}(m+\sigma/2).
\]

So the exact nonvanishing condition is simply
\[
\boxed{
-B^2\sigma^2\sin\Delta_0+3B\sigma\cos\Delta_0+3\sin\Delta_0\neq 0.
}
\]

That is already explicit. But there is a more informative small-\(\sigma\) expansion.

Since
\[
\Delta_0=-\int_{m-\sigma/2}^{m+\sigma/2} B_\zeta(t)\,dt,
\]
Taylor expansion gives
\[
\Delta_0
=
-B\sigma-\frac{B_\zeta''(m)}{24}\sigma^3+O(\sigma^5),
\]
because the odd terms integrate out symmetrically.

If you plug
\[
\Delta_0=-B\sigma+d_3\sigma^3+O(\sigma^5)
\]
into the numerator, the \(O(\sigma)\) and \(O(\sigma^3)\) terms coming from the pure constant-background part cancel, and the first surviving term is
\[
3d_3\sigma^3+O(\sigma^5).
\]
With
\[
d_3=-\frac{B_\zeta''(m)}{24},
\]
this gives
\[
c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)
=
-\frac{3}{4}\frac{B_\zeta''(m)}{B_\zeta(m)^4}
+
O(\sigma^2).
\]

So the real local condition is:

\[
\boxed{
c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)\neq 0 \text{ for small }\sigma
\quad\text{if}\quad
B_\zeta(m)\neq 0
\ \text{and}\ 
B_\zeta''(m)\neq 0.
}
\]

More precisely, if
\[
|B_\zeta''(m)|\ge b_2>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
B_\zeta(m)\asymp B_0>0
\]
on the midpoint class, then for \(\sigma\) small enough,
\[
|c_{\rm val}(m,\sigma)|\ge \frac{3b_2}{8B_0^4},
\]
after shrinking \(\sigma\) so the \(O(\sigma^2)\) remainder is smaller than half the main term.

So:

- **Yes**, we can derive an explicit analytic condition.
- **No**, we do not currently have a universal theorem that it always holds.
- What we *do* have is a clean sufficient condition: **nonzero background curvature** at the midpoint.

That is actually quite revealing. It says the value-calibration coefficient is not driven by the constant part of the background; that part cancels. It is driven by the **first nontrivial curvature correction** of the background phase gap.

So the next real question is:

> in the admissible midpoint class you want to use, can you prove \(B_\zeta''(m)\) stays bounded away from \(0\)?

If yes, then the \(\Phi_E\)-calibration is locked. If not, you may need to choose a different calibration functional \(\Psi\) whose leading term depends directly on \(B_\zeta(m)\) rather than on \(B_\zeta''(m)\).

That is the usable obstruction.

1. use \(\Phi_E\) to read off the leading value scale \(S(m)\),
2. use \(\Phi_K\) to show the zeta-side transverse component is only quadratic in \(S(m)\),

## User (2026-04-16 11:09:10)

determine whether this local comparison is by itself strong enough, or whether the old finite-s cancellation machinery is still indispensable.

## Assistant (2026-04-16 11:09:37)

_Thought for 15s_

It is **not** strong enough by itself.

The local comparison has become very sharp, but on its own it only gives a **jet-limit obstruction**. It says:

- toy off-line pair:
  \[
  \Phi_K(\Delta_{\rm mod}(u;d))=u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4),
  \qquad \Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0,
  \]
- zeta-side leading value channel:
  \[
  \Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta^{\rm lead})=0,
  \]
- therefore the zeta-side \(K\)-signal is pushed into the smaller remainder:
  \[
  \Phi_K(\Delta_\zeta)=O\!\bigl(L(m)S(m)^2\bigr)+O(\mathrm{Tail})+O(\mathrm{Err}).
  \]

That is a real structural mismatch. But by itself it is still only a **formal local asymptotic comparison**. It does not yet force a contradiction with the actual zeta/scattering object unless you can make three things rigorous:

1. the local matrix you are comparing really is the one produced by the true finite-\(s\) construction, not just its jet limit;
2. the tail/error terms are small enough on the relevant microscopic scale;
3. the calibration from the value channel to the toy parameter is legitimate in the actual analytic regime.

And those are exactly the places where the old finite-\(s\) cancellation machinery enters.

So the right verdict is:

## What the local comparison does give

It reduces the final obstruction to one scalar channel. That is a huge simplification. You no longer need a full matrix-plane theorem. You only need:

- one functional \(\Phi_E\) to calibrate the size of the value channel;
- one functional \(\Phi_K\) to detect the transverse toy anomaly.

That means the **conceptual** endgame is now local and finite-dimensional.

## What it does **not** give by itself

It does not by itself show that the true zeta-side local block at finite separation \(s\) inherits the same cancellation structure with sufficiently small remainder. The contradiction really needs statements of the form
\[
\Phi_E(\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m))=c_{\rm val}(m,s)\,S(m)+o(S(m)),
\]
and
\[
\Phi_K(\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m))=o(S(m)),
\]
uniformly on the microscopic scale. The jet-limit calculation strongly suggests these, but it does not replace the proof.

And that proof is exactly what the finite-\(s\) machinery was built to do:
- holomorphy on the \(Q^{-1}\)-disk,
- whitening control,
- oddness/cancellation,
- Cauchy coefficient bounds.

Without that package, the jet-limit comparison remains a persuasive model-side heuristic rather than a theorem about the actual zeta block.

## So is the old machinery indispensable?

For a **rigorous RH argument**: yes, probably indispensable.

For **guiding the final structure**: no, not conceptually indispensable anymore.

That is the important distinction.

The local comparison has told you what the old machinery must prove. It has changed the role of the finite-\(s\) package from “discover the obstruction” to “certify that the actual zeta object falls into the local obstruction regime.”

So the honest summary is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The local comparison is conceptually sufficient, but not yet rigorously sufficient.}
}
\]

You still need the finite-\(s\) analytic package to transfer the jet-limit obstruction to the actual zeta/scattering block with controlled error.

## The practical implication

If you want a paper that claims a genuine theorem in this direction, the next indispensable step is still the finite-\(s\) package — at least enough of it to show:

1. the value calibration through \(\Phi_E\) survives at finite \(s\),
2. the \(\Phi_K\)-cancellation survives at finite \(s\),
3. the remainder is \(o(S(m))\) on the microscopic scale.

If those are proved, then the local comparison is strong enough to finish the contradiction. If they are not, then the local comparison alone is not enough.

So the clean answer is: **the old finite-\(s\) cancellation machinery is still needed for rigor, but it is no longer the conceptual bottleneck.**

1. **Write the exact finite-\(s\) formulas** for the two scalar quantities
   \[
   \Phi_E(\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)),\qquad \Phi_K(\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)),

   \[
   \Phi_E(\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m))

4. Then show on your chosen microscopic regime that
   \[
   \text{tail}+\text{err}=o(S(m)).
   \]

That is the shortest route now.

So if I had to name one exact theorem to attack next, it would be:

> **Finite-\(s\) scalar transfer theorem.**  
> On the microscopic scale, \(\Phi_E\) reads the value channel linearly and \(\Phi_K\) kills it to first order, with remainder \(o(S(m))\).

That is the real next step.
## User (2026-04-16 11:24:34)

FYI read this: Yes. My best reconstruction is that they were already there in substance, under slightly different names.

The intended dictionary looks like this:

[
t_\pm = m \pm \frac{s}{2}.
]

At those two nearby points, you take the local two-dimensional **jet basis** — value and first derivative, or whatever your normalized jet pair is in the current convention. Then:

[
G_m(s)
]
is the **same-point jet Gram block**. In plain English: it measures how the local jet at (t_-) pairs with itself, and by symmetry the same formula is used for (t_+). That is why one symbol (G_m(s)) was enough under symmetric placement. This is exactly how the later checklist treats it: “the local jet Gram block (G_m(s))” whose holomorphy and (\partial_s G_m(s)=O(Q^2)) needed to be checked before whitening.  

[
N_m(s)
]
is the **cross jet block**. In plain English: it measures how the jet at (t_-) pairs with the jet at (t_+). Again, that is exactly how the notes use it: “the local jet cross block (N_m(s))” that gets whitened together with (G_m(s)).  

Then the normalized object was intended to be

[
\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)
=========================

G_m(s)^{-1/2} N_m(s) G_m(s)^{-1/2},
]

possibly followed by background subtraction / phase-gap subtraction depending on the precise stage of the argument. That formula appears repeatedly as the whole point of introducing (G_m(s)) and (N_m(s)): they are the raw pre-whitened blocks.  

So, in ELI5 terms:

* (G_m(s)) tells you what the local coordinate system looks like at the two nearby points.
* (N_m(s)) tells you how the two nearby points talk to each other.
* Whitening by (G_m(s)^{-1/2}) removes the local scaling/basis distortion so you can compare actual structure rather than coordinate artifacts.

That is why they feel so fundamental: they are basically the “bones” underneath the local statistic.

Where they seem to connect to the notation you already had is this. In the later jet-limit writeup, for two centers (T_1,T_2), you introduced

[
J_j=\frac1\pi M_j
]
for the local jet Gram matrices at each point, and

[
C_{12}=\frac1\pi N_{12}
]
for the cross-jet matrix, with
[
\Omega_\infty(T_1,T_2)=M_1^{-1/2}N_{12}M_2^{-1/2}.
]
That is almost certainly the **jet-limit avatar** of the same finite-(s) objects. In other words, (M_j) and (N_{12}) are not new ideas; they are what (G_m(s)) and (N_m(s)) become after you pass all the way to the explicit jet-limit formulas. 

So the likely intended hierarchy is:

* **finite (s)**: (G_m(s), N_m(s)) = raw local zeta/scattering jet blocks;
* **after whitening**: (\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)=G_m(s)^{-1/2}N_m(s)G_m(s)^{-1/2});
* **jet limit / explicit algebraic model**: (M_j, N_{12}, \Omega_\infty).  

And that explains the annoyance perfectly: the notes had the abstract role of (G_m(s)) and (N_m(s)) very clearly, and later had the explicit **limit** formulas (M_j,N_{12}), but seem never to have frozen the **finite-(s) exact entry formulas** in one canonical notation. The files themselves say that exact finite-(s) formulas for (G_m(s)) and (N_m(s)) are still the missing ingredient.  

So if I had to reconstruct the most likely intended definitions in one sentence:

[
G_m(s)=\text{the symmetric local same-point 2\times2 jet Gram block at }m\pm s/2,
]
[
N_m(s)=\text{the corresponding mixed left-right 2\times2 jet block},
]
and (\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)) is just their whitened cross block.

The only thing still missing is the exact finite-(s) formula for those blocks in the zeta/scattering normalization you settled on.

The next useful step is to reconstruct those formulas explicitly from the kernel notation you were already using, so you can see whether (G_m(s)) should really be called something like (G_{--}(m,s)) and (N_m(s)) something like (G_{-+}(m,s)) before symmetry collapses them.

## Assistant (2026-04-16 11:24:59)

_Thought for 15s_

Yes — that reconstruction is probably right, and it helps.

It says the missing finite-\(s\) formulas are not conceptually mysterious at all. They should just be the finite-separation versions of the jet-limit blocks you already wrote down:

- \(G_m(s)\): the same-point \(2\times2\) jet Gram block at \(t_-=m-s/2\) and, by symmetry, equivalently at \(t_+=m+s/2\),
- \(N_m(s)\): the mixed left-right \(2\times2\) jet block between \(t_-\) and \(t_+\),
- and
  \[
  \widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)=G_m(s)^{-1/2}N_m(s)G_m(s)^{-1/2}
  \]
  before or after the explicit renormalization terms, depending on stage.

That matches the jet-limit story perfectly:
\[
G_m(s)\rightsquigarrow J_j=\frac1\pi M_j,
\qquad
N_m(s)\rightsquigarrow C_{12}=\frac1\pi N_{12},
\qquad
\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)\rightsquigarrow \Omega_\infty(T_1,T_2).
\]

So the real next step is now clear and much less scary:

## Reconstruct the finite-\(s\) blocks directly from the kernel

Take the actual zeta/scattering phase kernel
\[
K_\Phi(x,y)=
\begin{cases}
\dfrac{\sin(\Phi(x)-\Phi(y))}{\pi(x-y)},&x\neq y,\\[1ex]
\dfrac{\Phi'(x)}{\pi},&x=y,
\end{cases}
\]
and define
\[
t_-:=m-\frac{s}{2},\qquad t_+:=m+\frac{s}{2}.
\]

Then the finite-\(s\) blocks should simply be the jet-basis transforms of the raw \(2\times2\) point blocks.

If
\[
A_{--}(m,s):=
\begin{pmatrix}
K(t_-,t_-) & K(t_-,t_-^{\,\prime})\\
K(t_-^{\,\prime},t_-) & K(t_-^{\,\prime},t_-^{\,\prime})
\end{pmatrix}
\]
is the local same-point block in raw nearby-point coordinates, and
\[
A_{-+}(m,s)
\]
the mixed block, then \(G_m(s)\) and \(N_m(s)\) should be obtained by the same point-to-jet change-of-basis matrix \(P_s\) you already identified in the jet-limit calculation:
\[
P_s=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
1&1\\[1ex]
-1/s&1/s
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

So the likely finite-\(s\) definitions are
\[
G_m(s)=P_s\,A_{--}(m,s)\,P_s^\top,
\qquad
N_m(s)=P_s\,A_{-+}(m,s)\,P_s^\top,
\]
with symmetry identifying the \(--\) and \(++\) local blocks.

That is exactly the finite-\(s\) version of the later jet-limit formulas.

## Why this matters

If this is right, then the remaining analytic package becomes much more manageable:

- holomorphy of \(G_m(s)\) and \(N_m(s)\) reduces to holomorphy of the kernel entries \(K_\Phi(t_\pm,t_\pm)\), \(K_\Phi(t_-,t_+)\), and their finite-difference quotients,
- the \(Q^{-1}\)-disk comes from keeping the denominators away from the zero/pole locations,
- the derivative bound
  \[
  \sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_GQ^2
  \]
  comes from differentiating those explicit kernel expressions plus the \(1/s\) factors in \(P_s\),
- and the \(s\to0\) limit recovers exactly the jet Gram matrix \(J(T)\) you already computed.

So this reconstruction is probably the missing bridge between the abstract finite-\(s\) notation and the explicit jet-limit formulas.

## The exact next move

The next thing to do is not another high-level theorem. It is to **write these reconstructed formulas out explicitly entry by entry**.

Concretely:

1. define the four raw kernel values
   \[
   K_{--}=K_\Phi(t_-,t_-),\quad
   K_{-+}=K_\Phi(t_-,t_+),\quad
   K_{+-}=K_\Phi(t_+,t_-),\quad
   K_{++}=K_\Phi(t_+,t_+);
   \]

2. apply the point-to-jet transform \(P_s\) to get explicit formulas for the entries of \(G_m(s)\) and \(N_m(s)\);

3. simplify those entries into combinations of
   \[
   \sin(\Phi(t_-)-\Phi(t_+)),\quad \cos(\Phi(t_-)-\Phi(t_+)),\quad q_\zeta(t_\pm),
   \]
   and powers of \(s\);

4. then check holomorphy and the derivative bound directly from those formulas.

That is now the right next step.
